Although sales to outside customers of 嚋昔暢成 were once brisk, they are also quite scarce at present, due to the impact of tight credit. There is no hope for any development in this street's business. Quotations for various goods have declined as a result. The recent trend of green lead, tinplate, black iron sheet, and galvanized iron sheet all show signs of being strong on the outside but weak on the inside. According to people in the industry, if one wants to see the development of the hardware future, it is feared that a large closing period is necessary.

Free Talk

Glimpses of the 19th Route Army 150

— Zhao

The Japanese pirates harassed Shanghai. Both Chinese and foreigners were indignant. Our 19th Route Army resisted them, lasting for a month. Annihilated 20,000 enemy troops, raising our country's international status and striving for national survival. Especially admired by the imperial court and the common people. Huang Gu, the commander of the 155th Brigade of the army, was intelligent and capable, planning strategies and often achieving unexpected victories. Here are some anecdotes of the brigade to see a glimpse of our army's resistance against Japan this time.

Soldiers Persuade Each Other to Practice Target Shooting Since the September 18th Incident, people have been panicked, and the whole country has been boiling. The soldiers of the brigade were also very angry and excited. Brigade Commander Huang Gu, in his spare time, lectured his troops on the facts of the Eastern Provinces being lost and exposed the Japanese ambitions to seize Manchuria. The soldiers were furious when they heard this, with the determination to break the cauldrons and sink the boats, hoping to fight to the death. During peacetime training, they became more diligent, especially in target shooting. In their target shooting, they first drew a human figure on the target with the words "Japanese" written on it. Then, they aimed at this target and shot. When a shot hit, they were all overjoyed, feeling relieved. They would either offer congratulatory remarks or shout anti-Japanese slogans.

Using Rice Bowls and Dishware to Repel the Enemy The enemy relied on the sophistication of their military equipment to attack us fiercely. However, most of their soldiers, raised in comfort and luxury, had no combat experience, so there were many who retreated in battle. On the evening of February 25th, more than 30 enemy soldiers came to spy on our positions. There were only three soldiers from the 155th Brigade stationed there. They were eating in the trenches when they saw the Japanese soldiers advancing. They didn't have time to raise their guns, so they took their rice bowls and dishes and threw them far away. Unexpectedly, the enemy soldiers were as timid as mice. They thought it was a hand grenade falling from the sky and quickly abandoned their armor and weapons and fled. We also let them go without chasing them, only clapping our hands and laughing.

Squad Leader Single-Handedly Seizes a New Gun During the Battle of Zhu Yuan Dun on February 25th, the enemy fired a series of shots. The sound was unusual, never heard before. Chen Youzhi, the squad leader of the 2nd Regiment of the brigade, had been in the army for a long time and was capable in battle. He figured it was the enemy's newest weapon and wanted to get it. At that time, the 5th Company of the regiment also wanted to seize this new killing weapon and charged bravely, sacrificing many. At night, the squad leader took advantage of the dim night and crept in from the side, sneaking into the enemy camp. Several enemy gunmen were asleep. So he killed them one by one and seized the gun to return. According to enemy prisoners, the gun was called a "helmet machine gun," the latest Japanese invention, light and sharp, and could not be compared with other guns. This was the first time it was used on the battlefield.

[P The Modern World

— Translated by Yi

What exactly is a modern world?

It is a playground. In every field, there shines a light of hypocrisy. With irony and ridicule, they perform dramas of the remnants of justice and morality that people consider to be outdated.

It is a conservatory of music. The sounds of cheering and booing drown out all the music. One cannot tell whether the musician's tune is correct or whether the rhythm of the instruments is in sync.

It is a large casino. Dice and playing cards fly everywhere. Throughout the hall, we can vaguely and intermittently hear the triumphant laughter and disappointed sighs of gamblers.

It is a grand banquet. On the ceiling, many sharp swords hang by thin threads. Each sword has a guest sitting beneath it, and an invisible hand writes terrifying words on the wall. But all the guests calmly and carelessly drink wildly.

It is a store. Even the dust inside is worth a golden price. They all trade with each other using deception and fraud.

It is a maze. No matter how nimble you are and how you follow the guiding thread from the past, you can walk a hundred circles in the crossroads and never find the way out you imagined.

It is a sea full of reefs. Although it is a calm and tranquil ocean, shipwrecks and sunken ships lie everywhere. Because the light illuminating the lighthouses in the sea completely deceives the eyes of sailors. The anchors cannot be cast on the soft mud on the seabed. The ship circles on the turbulent water, unable to move forward or backward. The boatman peers at the afterglow of the setting sun, panicking and bewildered. Looking ahead, he does not know where to find his final destination in the vast ocean.

Scraps of Thought 151

— Da Wei

Those with guns say, "I can't beat him"; those without guns say, "I can't hit him." So they have to be slaughtered!

The Chinese are most brave in fighting the Chinese, no wonder the Japanese want to drive the Chinese to fight the Chinese.

A part of the people are shouting "National crisis is imminent," and many people are indifferent because the "national crisis" is on the heads of a part of the people, behind the brains of a part of the people.

When the September 18th Incident occurred, other ordinary people said, "The people of the Northeast are suffering." When the January 28th Incident occurred, other ordinary people said, "The people of Shanghai are suffering." These ordinary people do not seem to have thought that the people of the Northeast and Shanghai are their own compatriots, let alone that their own positions are the same as those of the Northeast and Shanghai.

The Record of the Twin Towers in the Military Horses 152

Seeking Happiness, Master Qi (36)

—

Chapter 5: Betrayal and Severance of Friendship Unluckily Encountering a Generous Guest, Anger is Bound, and Deliberating Strategy is Most Difficult to Endure, the Beauty's Favor

Unexpectedly, that night at midnight, the camp was in an uproar. A battalion of soldiers arrived to suppress bandits, calling to open the camp gate to come in and search for the bandit leader, Niu Heifeng. An Dacheng inquired with the battalion commander leading the team, and it turned out that An Dakui had called them. Because the military headquarters was offering a heavy reward for the capture of Niu Heifeng. An Dakui had long wanted to be promoted to a substantive military officer but had no opportunity. So he did not hesitate to sell out his friend for glory and reported to the garrison headquarters. He had also brought another battalion of troops to provide backup. He initially thought that if Niu Heifeng entered his Anjia Camp, he would have to stay at least one night. Wouldn't that be like a turtle in a jar, easily captured and sent to claim the credit? He did not expect Niu Heifeng to fall for this trick, which made him miss. An Dacheng heard this and was greatly dissatisfied, only scolding him for acting absurdly and not leaving any room for maneuver. He had not consulted at all beforehand before randomly asking for troops. Fortunately, Niu Heifeng had already left, and there had been no conflict between the two sides. Even if he caught Niu Heifeng with a cold stab and achieved his goal of promotion and wealth, Niu Heifeng would not have spared me before being caught. The good Anjia Camp would have been ruined by him, first suffering the calamity of the fish in the pond. When An Dakui failed to capture Niu Heifeng and heard that An Dacheng was blaming him, he did not return to the camp. He quietly withdrew his troops and returned. Even more unexpectedly, Niu Heifeng's ears and eyes were very sharp. The secret agents he had sent out had already swiftly reported these things to Niu Heifeng. Upon hearing this, Niu Heifeng became furious, thinking that the Anjia brothers were not enough friends. Since they were not kind, he would not be righteous. He immediately gathered six or seven hundred bandits. Taking advantage of the fact that the government troops had not gone far, he turned around and returned to Anjia Camp. An Dacheng knew things were bad, but he thought there was still room for explanation. He still ordered the group to open the camp gate and let them in. He did not expect that Niu Heifeng was now harboring resentment and no longer recognized anyone. Outside the camp gate, he shouted loudly and first captured An Dacheng. Then, a swarm of people rushed into the camp, killing people indiscriminately and burning houses upon seeing them. Pitifully, An Dacheng was implicated by his brother and died under the bandits' random gunfire before he could say a word. When the house caught fire, An Da's wife and family members were also burned to death. Only a loyal long-term worker rescued An Yuyuan in the emergency, hiding him in the cabbage field behind the house to avoid the disaster.

This Newspaper's Local Supplement 153

Talking and Saying

On the Rumor of Pu Yi's Assassination in Changchun 154

Yesterday, I saw in the newspaper a report from Shenyang that "Pu Yi was assassinated in Changchun, but not fatally wounded. The reason was his refusal to sign the new Japan-Manchukuo treaty, leading to a warning from the Japanese faction." Whether this news is accurate is still unknown. Assuming this is indeed the case, some say it is Pu Yi's good fortune, but I say it is Pu Yi's great misfortune.

Some say that Pu Yi is still clear-headed, enjoys reading, and has quite modern ideas. This time, a new farce was staged in the Northeast, partly due to his being kidnapped by the Japanese and partly due to the restoration dreams of a bunch of sycophants. I don't entirely believe this, but perhaps there is some truth to it. If it were true that Pu Yi was assassinated in Changchun, it would be excellent proof that Pu Yi's conscience was not entirely lost. We could all forgive him and mourn him.

If he was not assassinated, then he is living a life of torment. In name, he is the head of state, but in reality, he has not a shred of sovereignty, being entirely a puppet. What difference is there between such a head of state and being imprisoned? Looking back at our entire history, has any monarch who lost his country survived unscathed? Yet, when the Qing Dynasty abdicated, not only was he not harmed, but he was also given royal treatment and expenses of several million yuan per year. Now, because the country's finances are exhausted, this payment has been canceled. But the Republic's treatment of Pu Yi can truly be called benevolent and righteous. Pu Yi should think about it and be moved to tears of gratitude.

Therefore, I deeply fear that this news is inaccurate, and if it is accurate, I even more deeply regret that he did not die.

Popular Literature 155

Miscellaneous Poems on Luoyang by Xu Ying

The aura of kingship in the southeast has long faded away,

Hairpins of gold lie scattered, no longer in rows.

The beacon fires of Lord Chunshen rise to the heavens,

A blue canopy hurriedly enters Luoyang.

The palaces of Luoyang, a desolate, cold mist,

In the desolate world, years pass.

Suddenly, news arrives of a court assembly in spring,

The east wind brings a night of blooming flowers.

Looking south to Chunshen, already three thousand li,

No alarms sound, sleeping peacefully in broad daylight.

Still calling Chang'an a secondary capital,

Planning to flee further west to avoid the barbarians.

The spring waters of Jin Bridge surpass the waves of Wu,

More beautiful than the sights of Jinling.

Fleeing west, only seeking to evade the invaders,

Moreover, hearing of a comfortable place to settle.

What is the use of a million heroic troops,

Hanging their hands, heading southeast to surrender?

From now on, the principle is non-resistance,

Unexpectedly, Qin Hui is the one who knew best.

Returning to reside once more on the western coast,

Scheming and vying for power, desires fulfilled.

Yet laughing that an official post can cause illness,

The governor alone can claim a thousand autumns.

Slandering Niu and ousting Li, wasting effort on management,

High salaries and official positions, matters finally settled.

The ambition to restore the Central Plains is ultimately abandoned,

Only now realizing that Yin Hao was just empty words.

The petty man changes his face but not his heart,

The flawed lineage is passed down, is it just today?

Neither fighting, surrendering, nor fleeing,

You gentlemen are still ashamed of Ye Mingchen.

The gathered heroes fly to the Western Palace,

Striving to devise plans to defend the nation from calamity.

Alas, the courtyard is full of empty, good ideas,

Spring comes, always delaying the beauty's rainbow.

Entrusting the rise and fall of the former kingdom to mournful poems,

Banners and flags seen in the distance, barbarian clouds deep.

In what year will the halberd be drawn to pass through three households,

The old men of Chu meet, tears filling their sleeves.

Popular Science 156

Glass Ceramics by Xiao Tao

Glass is extremely useful to mankind. On a small scale, it can help people see microorganisms that are invisible to the naked eye; on a large scale, it can help people study stars hundreds of millions of light-years away. Each light-year equals six trillion miles, because light travels six trillion miles in a year. Telescopes made of glass can allow people to see stars six trillion trillion miles away. To put it more simply, glass windows allow light to enter the room but prevent flies from coming in to make trouble. What a wonderful invention! The uses of everyday lampshades, bottles, and cups are also obvious. Since the functions of glass are so great, how can we not know its history and manufacturing?

Several thousand years ago, the Egyptians were already making glass, but the glass they made was not very good, even less transparent than today's dark glass bottles. By the fifteenth century, the Phoenicians in Europe could make transparent glass, but it was only used to make decorations for a few nobles, and its value was simply more precious than gold.

Its manufacturing method commonly involves mixing limestone, sodium carbonate, and silica sand (also known as silicon dioxide) and then burning it in a kiln. When heated to about 200 degrees Celsius, the mixture melts into a transparent liquid, which becomes a solid when cooled, i.e., glass. While in liquid form, a long blowpipe about five feet long is dipped into it, and then it is blown into a circle with the mouth. The blowpipe is cut off from the blown glass item, and then it is placed in a greenhouse to let it cool gradually so that it is very strong. If it cools down suddenly, it is easily broken. If we want to blow bottles of various shapes, then a mold is essential. Dip a little glass liquid with the blowpipe into the mold, and blow it to produce something that is the same as the mold. Ordinary glass for making chemical equipment contains potassium salt, and the resulting glass is hard, called hard glass. Glass made with sodium salt is softer, called soft glass, and can be used to make glass for doors and windows. Glass made with lead oxide instead of limestone is soft and has a high refractive index, making it suitable for optical instruments such as lenses. Glass for glass windows is made by blowing the glass liquid into a long cylindrical shape, cutting it in the middle, and then flattening it. Glass items that come out of the mold are very rough, but they can be modified at will. The glass industry in China has gradually developed. Jinan in Shandong and Zhabei in Shanghai both have small-scale glass factories. Visiting them nearby can broaden one's knowledge a lot.

Casual Talk 157

The Tragic Encounter of the No. 8 Oriole

A small group of refugees was walking slowly on a certain road in western Shanghai. In the crowd, they were regarded as a kind of subhuman animal.

They walked across Zhongshan Bridge, turned back northwest, gradually moving away from the noisy Shanghai. When they passed the first village, they smelled the breath of the new spring and saw the green plants. This made them feel as if they had escaped from the high-pressure air, so they quickened their pace.

Indeed, they couldn't even afford a wheelbarrow for a dollar. They were prepared to walk the more than fifty li of the long journey on their two legs, so they had to take advantage of rest to recover from their fatigue.

After passing the railway, they began to encounter groups of farmers fleeing towards Shanghai. Occasionally, one or two fellow villagers were mixed in, and they would stop and chat for a few words. Those who were closer would advise them to turn back, describing one or two fresh events in a terrifying tone. In the end, they would add a sentence... ["Going back to hell, you?"]

Among them was a thrifty middle-aged farmer, clutching his tears, murmuring in reply to them: ["What can we do? The refugee camps are just as much hell. We might as well go back to our own village to die."]

This was a remote, isolated village. Apart from a few crows cawing, not even a live dog could be found in the village. There were two or three Japanese slogans on the broken walls, stripped of their corners, blowing in the wind. Although the houses still existed, there was no longer a single complete thing in the houses. Everything was messy straw, torn clothes, and destroyed doors, windows, and furniture.

Now, they were trapped in the deep abyss of despair. Faintly, voices came closer from the distance. They heard them very clearly. This was a very unusual sound. Everyone stood up in shock and secretly ran to the outside of the threshing ground. Suddenly, on the eastern corner of the village's harvest field, three soldiers appeared who were not from our country. This shocking discovery caused them to lose consciousness.

A sinister laugh mixed with a string of "Ji Ge Ji Ge" words. At first, they patted the women's shoulders and tapped the women's small feet with the butts of their guns. Then, they gestured, wanting them to take off their clothes together. They clasped their trembling hands in a bow, but this was ineffective.

Finally, they tied up the two men who were almost dead from anger and terror and threw them one by one onto the harvest field. Then, they dragged a woman each into the house.

When the sun emitted its last ray of light in the western sky, the three bestial men left. Only then did they struggle out.

In this way, they decided on their plan to leave again tomorrow. All the feelings of shame, anger, and terror turned into tears.

East, West, North, South 158

The Home of Officials by Wu

The only reason I ran to Mrs. Li's house today was to pay a visit as a friend. As soon as I walked in, I heard the lively sound of mahjong tiles. I thought, "I've come at a good time, or else I'd have to fill in for one of them when they were 'one short.' But today, everyone is here, so they probably won't need me to give them money for cigarettes." Sure enough, when the insignificant me appeared before her, she only said seemingly apologetically:

"Sorry, we're playing mahjong again... Lotus... bring tea and cigarettes for the guest!"

Then a lovely young maid served tea and cigarettes.

Before long, the mahjong game ended. Mrs. Li's mahjong luck was really good. In front of her was a neat pile of copper coins and several silver dollars. As soon as she got up, she called me to her "opium den." A maid had already prepared the opium pipe and was waiting for her. So she lazily lay down. After yawning, she revealed her dark teeth with a smile and said:

"Today, I really invited the God of Wealth." I won the "flower game," and I also won quite a few copper coins playing mahjong."

"Good luck, good luck!... What did the 'flower game' pay out today?" I asked to join in the fun, because this would definitely make her very happy.

"I dreamt last night that there was no more war, and today, it actually paid out 'Peace.' Isn't that really strange?" "Ah! Mrs. Li's dreams are really accurate. When will I get to benefit from your good fortune and bet a few copper coins with you?" I guessed correctly, this pleased her very much, but she didn't have time to laugh, because she was already sucking on that thick opium pipe.

From her conversation, I learned that Mr. Li had gone from Guangdong to Luoyang to participate in the so-called important, crucial national crisis conference. She could have taken this opportunity to see the peonies in "Temporary Capital" (because all the hospitality expenses are paid by the government), but because Mr. Li took a woman who had gone from being a private secretary to becoming a concubine with him, this made her feel embarrassed, so she was happy to relax at home. However, Mr. Li had sent quite a bit of money since going to Luoyang and was confident of securing a very profitable position, which made Mrs. Li smile from ear to ear.

"I heard that there's going to be another war in Shanghai. What should we do?" she suddenly asked worriedly, so I also echoed her and said:

"That's not going to happen. That's right, Mrs. Li! Tomorrow, 'Nine Officials' or 'Ten Thousand Gold' are very good characters to bet on."

Bits and Pieces 159

A Sketch of Xiao Te's Funeral by Lao Tang

A sky covered with dark clouds enveloped everything. The wide Jing'an Temple Road was crowded with spectators watching the "Grand Funeral Procession." The "Sando Tou" and "Ah San" faces were covered with beads of "calling customs" sweat. The movie cameras and tens of thousands of eyes were waiting eagerly, like waiting for rain in a great drought, for the arrival of the coffin of the righteous warrior Xiao Te who sacrificed for humanity and justice!

From one o'clock to two o'clock and even three o'clock and four o'clock, after several rounds of light rain, hope finally became a reality.

Boy Scouts with tilted hats passed through our line of sight with the ding-a-ling of bicycle bells, followed by cars carrying wreaths, cars carrying coffins, cars carrying Girl Scouts, cars carrying foreign men and women, cars following cars, cars still following cars.

After a group of green mourners disappeared from the audience's eyes, those who had raised their heads retracted them, and the people standing in the middle of the road retreated to the sidewalk. Finally, the character dismantler at the entrance of Jing'an Temple, after touching his mustache several times, stepped down from his special box-like stool.

On the way home, I heard two kinds of voices:

"Nothing to see!"

"If I had known it would be like this, who would have been happy to wait three or four hours!"

After returning home and looking at the newspaper on my desk, I realized that I hadn't looked "carefully" just now. It turned out that the newspaper clearly stated that the procession would "turn around at Xiaoshadu Road." I asked the people who watched at the entrance of Hardoon Garden, and they said they saw three bands.

Shanghai Second Special District Local Court 163

Criminal Judgments: Police Department vs. Wang Qingdong and Others Opium Case (Main Text): Wang Qingdong is sentenced to six months imprisonment for providing a venue for others to smoke opium substitutes. Wang Asi, Cai Agen, Liu Ar'er, Gu Zhen, Chen Qian Shi, and Lu Suzhen are sentenced to one month imprisonment for smoking opium substitutes. Pre-trial detention days shall be converted at a rate of two days for each day of imprisonment. Chen Qian Shi and Lu Suzhen are each granted a two-year suspended sentence. Seven opium pipes and one tael of red pills are confiscated and burned according to the list. Police Department vs. Wang Shuizhen and Others Opium Case (Main Text): Wang Shuizhen is sentenced to six months imprisonment for providing a venue for others to smoke opium substitutes. Chen Jinhai, Xu Tang Shi, Li Xuerong, Shen Jinlin, Zhang Guohua, and Bian Qingtang are each sentenced to one month imprisonment for smoking opium substitutes. Pre-trial detention days shall be converted at a rate of two days for each day of imprisonment. Opium pipes, red pills, etc., are all confiscated and burned. Police Department vs. Wang Degui and Others Opium Case (Main Text): Wang Degui is sentenced to six months imprisonment for providing a venue for others to smoke opium substitutes. Xiong Wenshan and Peng Jiachun are each sentenced to two months imprisonment for smoking opium substitutes. Pre-trial detention days shall be converted at a rate of two days for each day of imprisonment. Xiong Wenshan and Peng Jiachun are each granted a two-year suspended sentence. Opium pipes and red pills are confiscated and burned according to the list. Police Department vs. Tan Ma Shi Opium Case (Main Text): Tan Ma Shi is sentenced to one month imprisonment for smoking opium and fined sixty yuan. If the fine cannot be paid, it shall be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Pre-trial detention days shall be converted at a rate of one day for every two yuan of the fine. Opium pipes, opium lamps, opium needles, opium trays, etc., are all confiscated and burned. Police Department vs. Jiang Xitang Opium Case (Main Text): Jiang Xitang is fined one hundred yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. If the fine cannot be paid, it shall be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Pre-trial detention days shall be converted at a rate of one day for every two yuan of the fine. Opium pipes, opium lamps, opium needles, opium trays, etc., are all confiscated and burned. Police Department vs. Yang Zhang Shi Opium Case (Main Text): Yang Zhang Shi is fined sixty yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. If the fine cannot be paid, it shall be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Pre-trial detention days shall be converted at a rate of one day for every two yuan of the fine. Opium pipes, opium lamps, opium needles, opium tongs, opium trays, opium bubbles, etc., are all confiscated and burned. Police Department vs. Yu Zhenfa Opium Case

(Main Text): Yu Zhenfa is fined forty yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. If the fine cannot be paid, it shall be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Zhu Ronglin's stolen goods case (Main Text): Zhu Ronglin is sentenced to 40 days of detention for knowingly purchasing stolen goods, and the detention days shall be converted at a rate of two days for one day of detention.

Automobile News

Commentary

Current State of the British Automobile Industry 165

Sluggish Sales of American Cars

Although the automobile manufacturing industry in Britain is considered developed in Europe, there is a vast disparity in output compared to the United States. Therefore, British-made cars are insufficient to meet the needs of the country and its colonies. Consequently, American-made cars have held a significant position in the British market. In recent times, the European economic situation has deteriorated drastically, with all industries declining and people facing great hardship. To protect their interests, various countries have used different methods to promote the development of domestic industries and encourage citizens to buy domestically produced goods. Hence, Britain has adopted the slogan "Buy British Goods," which has had some impact.

Last year, the number of cars shipped from the United States to Britain for sale was only 3,330 units, a significant decline compared to previous years. Two years ago, in 1930, 10,694 American-made cars were sold in Britain, and in 1929, the number was even higher, totaling 22,729 units. Comparing these three figures, the rise and fall can be clearly seen. Considering just December of last year, the total number of cars and chassis manufactured in the United States and shipped to Britain for sale was only 80 units. In the same period in 1929, there were as many as 1,019 units.

The reasons why American cars have not sold well in Britain have been mentioned above. Additionally, there is another significant reason: the implementation of horsepower taxation and the popularity of small cars. Horsepower taxation is based on the engine's horsepower to determine the tax to be paid. The import tax on foreign-made cars is also very high, deterring potential buyers. As for large British-made cars, their sales have become even more sluggish, as those with 20, 30, or 40 horsepower are subject to extremely high taxes, leading to a lack of demand. Consequently, the resale of old cars does not fetch a good price. Recently, a Dutch merchant in Britain purchased over 400 old British cars and shipped them to the Netherlands, as there is no horsepower taxation there.

To avoid horsepower taxation, British car manufacturers have been striving to produce and sell small cars, generally with 9, 10, or 15 horsepower. At the last British Motor Show, 12 car dealerships showcased small cars. These cars are often referred to as "baby cars," with most having horsepower exceeding 10. The advantage of small cars is not only avoiding high taxes but also their significant economic benefits, such as fuel savings and reduced costs. Therefore, they have become popular, with many people abandoning large cars for smaller ones. In the past two months, the exact number of British car sales within the country is unknown, but it is estimated to be around 138,000 units, while American car sales are only about 4,200 units. This is a far cry from the 155,000 units in 1930. On the export side, due to the devaluation of the pound, there has been improvement, with 18,992 units last year compared to 23,210 units in 1930. In the last two months of last year, November and December, the devaluation of the pound was particularly advantageous, with 4,560 cars exported, compared to only 4,119 units in the same period in 1930.

British car dealerships and manufacturers are fiercely competing with American car sales. Many American car factories have established plants in Britain to manufacture cars. According to a survey last year, the commercial vehicles sold by these American factories are entirely manufactured in Britain and exported to various British territories, resulting in substantial profits. Another car factory, with half of its products manufactured in Britain, experienced a 10% decline in sales due to commercial recession. The sales of British-made commercial vehicles last year are estimated to be around 50,000 units.

In 1931, the total number of British cars sold in New Zealand was 2,414 units, worth £272,285, while the sales of American cars were only 475 units, worth $59,975. American car sales in Africa were also significantly lower, and the situation in Ceylon was similar. British car sales in these two regions were quite brisk. In Australia, due to various factors, car imports have generally declined, but the sales of British-made cars in Australia increased to 50.7% in the first six months of 1931, compared to only 17% in the same period in 1930. Therefore, the outlook for the British car export industry is optimistic.

Reflections on the Automotive Industry in Soviet Russia 166

The automotive industry is a significant asset in war, which readers have probably long realized. Since the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, the situation in the Far East has become increasingly tense, with newspaper reports suggesting that Russia and Japan are busily preparing for war, creating a sense of imminent conflict. Therefore, readers are keen to know the current state of the automotive industry in Soviet Russia. Below is a record of Soviet Russia's recent plans and progress in the automotive industry to inform this publication.

Although industry in Soviet Russia has been developing rapidly, there has been a lack of automobile manufacturing plants. The cars used in Russia were originally imported from the United States. However, recently, the Soviet authorities, recognizing the importance of the automotive industry to the national economy, people's livelihood, and military preparedness, have decided to implement domestic automobile manufacturing. Most of the automobile factories that were under construction have now been completed. Not long ago, the first Soviet-made car was successfully produced, and newspapers and magazines widely reported this event as a celebration. Soon, the second Soviet-made car will be available on the market. Currently, cars are being manufactured only in temporary factories, producing about five cars per day. However, all the parts are imported from the United States. Therefore, the cars currently produced in Soviet Russia are better described as "assembled" rather than "made." The automobile factories planned by the Soviet Union are no different from the largest, most modern automobile factories in Detroit, USA. In fact, we have seen many such factories. From another perspective, once Soviet Russia can manufacture cars independently, producing a thousand cars per day will not be difficult. It is only a matter of time. From the day the first car is produced to the completion of the automotive industry, there will be different stages of development, proceeding according to plan. The current factories aim to produce 400 cars per day, which is the highest goal. It is hoped that certain parts of the cars can be manufactured domestically. The progress is planned in five-year increments. In the first two years, all parts will be imported from the United States, with only assembly being done locally. By the end of the third year, at least half of the parts should be manufactured domestically. By the end of the fourth year, about 75% should be domestic. By the end of the fifth year, everything needed for the cars should be manufactured domestically, without relying on supplies from the United States. The construction of the factory buildings is entirely based on the form of the Cleveland Austin Car Factory. After the completion of this factory, all future work will not depend on others. Even the water supply will be provided by artesian wells. In this new factory, various machines have not yet been purchased, so the arrangement methods have not yet been determined. Once the machines are purchased, the arrangement will be done according to the form. Before the machines were ordered, the United States, Germany, and Britain were all competing for the business in Soviet Russia. Therefore, under these circumstances, it is not yet determined which country's products Soviet Russia will purchase in the future. Starting from November 1st last year, work has been intensified to expedite the completion of the factory buildings. It is expected that after completion, the interior will house at least 6,000 motors, and the scale will be impressive. The number of workers in this massive factory will undoubtedly be large. Therefore, the factory has decided to build worker housing. In this housing area, there will be hotels, parks, municipal halls, hospitals, schools, and all other facilities related to worker life. The plan is to build 300 four-story brick buildings, each housing 200 families. Upon completion, it will be like a new town.

Safety of the New Studebaker Car 167

The new Studebaker car has numerous features, but its most prominent feature is its safety construction. Among vehicles in the medium price range, there is no car like the new Studebaker that has so many safety features providing ample protection. Here are the most noteworthy safety features: The new Studebaker car, regardless of its style, comes standard with safety glass for its windshield and windows, without extra charge. This glass is clear as a mirror and unaffected by moisture. It is made by combining two layers with a thick, transparent material. Even in the event of a violent impact, it will only crack and not shatter, as the fragments stick to the laminated layer. This is further enhanced by the all-steel welded body construction, which provides even greater safety. The excellent chassis construction is also a major reason for Studebaker's absolute safety. The chassis has a double drop frame, and the body is mounted exquisitely and appropriately. The front and rear wheels are also particularly widened, so the center of gravity is lowered, and the entire car operates smoothly and without vibration. Other features, such as improved free-wheeling, automatic driving management, automatic choke, safety steel-core steering wheel, and new reflector taillights, all provide passengers and drivers with safety and enjoyment.

Statistics

Last Year's U.S. Car Sales Statistics Praised 168

According to recent official statistics obtained locally, the total number of new passenger cars registered in the United States in 1931 was 1,908,016 units. Car sales in that year fell by 700,000 units compared to 1930. The number of cars sold in the United States in the previous year was 2,626,068 units. Currently, leaders in the automotive manufacturing industry have different views on the future of the industry this year. Some giants and leaders predict that the number of used car sales this year will greatly benefit car sales in the United States, reaching 3,000,000 units. This is the optimistic estimate. The second group, the conservatives, predict that the minimum car sales will be around 2,000,000 units. Others say that car sales this year will be approximately between 2,500,000 and 3,000,000 units.

Of the total number of cars sold in the United States, Chevrolet, manufactured by General Motors, was the champion, with a total of 583,387 units. Ford came in second, with a ratio of 9 to 10. According to last year's statistics, Chevrolet's sales accounted for one-third of all car sales in the United States. Plymouth was the first in this class of cars to use free-wheeling construction and have "floating" power. Last year's sales unexpectedly increased greatly, ranking third in total car sales in the United States.

In 1930, Buick and Pontiac ranked third and fourth in American car sales. In 1931, Plymouth jumped to third place above Buick and Pontiac, which is a rare phenomenon in recent times. Plymouth is a product of Chrysler Motors and sells widely in Eastern countries. Buick still maintains its original position among its peers with similar prices. Although its sales seem weaker than in 1930, its reputation is still good. In 1931, Plymouth made rapid progress, pushing Pontiac from fourth to fifth place. Ford's products were completely new, with the introduction of new four-cylinder and eight-cylinder cars, which was quite sensational. However, its sales in 1931 fell the most. Miscellaneous

British Automotive Industry Tycoon 169

Henry Royce's Biography

Earl Henry Royce is a famous automobile manufacturer. The outstanding performance of the British seaplane in winning the Schneider Trophy and achieving a record of 400 miles per hour was due to the internal machinery manufactured by Royce. The Standard "Swallow" car, which is not scheduled to arrive in Shanghai,

The British Standard cars managed by the China Motor Company have arrived, including the Standard "Little Nine," Standard "Big Nine," Standard "Nineteen," and Standard "Twenty." These four types of cars are well received by all sectors of society. It is recently heard that there is also a Standard "Swallow" car that is not scheduled to arrive in Shanghai. This car is a specially low-built two-seater roadster, with a large luggage compartment behind the car body, making it a modern and practical sports car.

Therefore, he has made great contributions to it. Like other American and British automotive kings, their families were mostly poor before their success. For example, Ford in the United States was a craftsman in his early years, John Willys was a repair clerk, and Earl Austin of Britain was a technician's apprentice in his youth. Earl Morris started as a machinist. However, Earl Henry's environment was even worse. Reading his biography, it is known that it was even more difficult for him to reach his current position. He was orphaned at the age of nine. The following year, he became a newsboy in London, earning his own living. From the age of fourteen to seventeen, he entered a railway factory as an apprentice. After graduating, he entered the Lee Manufacturing Bureau. Soon after, he transferred to a tool factory, earning two dollars and seventy-five cents a week for 54 hours of hard work.

He only received three years of education, but he had a wealth of knowledge in electrical engineering. Therefore, he was employed by the London Electric Light Company. Unfortunately, the company went bankrupt when he was only nineteen years old.

He was not deterred by the setback, and he used his meager savings to open a small Royce company, specializing in the manufacture of arc light bulbs. However, this business did not generate much income, so in 1884, he began manufacturing power generators. Suddenly, cotton mills, ships, and local factories began to use generators, and the demand increased greatly. However, in 1900, prices fell slightly due to the colonial war.

At that time, Royce bought a car to save time and money, but he was greatly disappointed because the car was unreliable and noisy. Therefore, Henry brought the car into the factory and dismantled it completely to see how it was made.

Soon, he planned to build his own car, improving the engine and removing noise. In 1903, he succeeded. However, the car was small, with only ten horsepower. However, it was valued by Rolls. They agreed to manufacture cars in Manchester. As the supply could not meet the demand, they expanded to Derby and opened a Rolls-Royce company.

Initially, they only raised 50,000 yuan in capital, and the architect used 5,000 yuan. Royce also personally designed the first building, which still exists today. The factory was completed and opened in 1906.

Today, Earl Henry is still a director, major shareholder, and chief technician of the company. He completes the Rolls-Royce engine, he designs and manufactures the machines, which enabled the British Air Force to defeat Germany in the last World War, and he manufactures the interior of the aircraft, which enabled John Alcock and Arthur Brown to successfully fly across the Atlantic for the first time. He also plans and manufactures the engines to be particularly effective, which helped the British Royal Air Force win three consecutive Schneider Trophy victories.

In 1930, Henry Royce was ennobled as a baronet. At the celebration banquet last year, he was very humble, saying, "In the early years of struggle, the general technicians and foremen were more meritorious than I."

His actions can be represented by the motto on the door of the Derby factory: "Why are we poor? Because we are wasteful, especially in wasting time." (Remuneration for Relief)
